## Section 001: Python Reliability Reference Patterns
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Python Reliability Reference Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed title does not define how to select and combine Python reliability controls for a script, package, service, CLI, or async worker with different failure and compatibility risks
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Python Reliability Reference Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because Python's dynamic flexibility moves many defects to runtime; explicit boundaries and lifecycle tests localize uncertainty without pretending annotations validate data or that one tool guarantees reliability
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Python Reliability Reference Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: annotations are treated as validation, broad handlers hide faults or cancellation, mutable defaults share state, blocking work stalls async execution, imports perform irreversible work, or a new quality stack ignores existing CI and compatibility
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Python Reliability Reference Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use this reference for general Python reliability decisions and route framework, database, security, performance, or deployment specifics to dedicated evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Python Reliability Reference Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add a risk classifier, causal control stack, lightweight alternatives, failure counterexamples, compatibility boundaries, operational examples, and a claim-linked verification packet
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Python Reliability Reference Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that reliability comes from converting dynamic uncertainty into explicit boundaries and owned lifecycles, not from maximizing annotations or tool count
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Python Reliability Reference Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to parse untrusted inputs before domain logic, contain `Any`, model stable values explicitly, depend on protocols, distinguish expected outcomes from exceptional failures, own cleanup, preserve cancellation, avoid import effects, and test failures through the repository's existing gates
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Python Reliability Reference Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because Python's dynamic flexibility moves many defects to runtime; explicit boundaries and lifecycle tests localize uncertainty without pretending annotations validate data or that one tool guarantees reliability
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Python Reliability Reference Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; annotations are treated as validation, broad handlers hide faults or cancellation, mutable defaults share state, blocking work stalls async execution, imports perform irreversible work, or a new quality stack ignores existing CI and compatibility
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Python Reliability Reference Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: use this reference for general Python reliability decisions and route framework, database, security, performance, or deployment specifics to dedicated evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Python Reliability Reference Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add a risk classifier, causal control stack, lightweight alternatives, failure counterexamples, compatibility boundaries, operational examples, and a claim-linked verification packet

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Python Reliability Reference Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: annotations are treated as validation, broad handlers hide faults or cancellation, mutable defaults share state, blocking work stalls async execution, imports perform irreversible work, or a new quality stack ignores existing CI and compatibility
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Python Reliability Reference Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: the boundary is important because the main risks are `Any` spreading inward, catching `Exception` and returning `None`, `assert` on external input, forgotten encodings, logs leaking secrets, monkeypatching production design, tests that miss cleanup, and adopting APIs unsupported by declared Python versions
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Python Reliability Reference Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: crossing one boundary does not invalidate the default where the repository's Python targets and toolchain are known, public contracts and runtime edges are identifiable, resource ownership is explicit, and fixtures can exercise success, error, timeout, cancellation, import, and packaging behavior

- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Python Reliability Reference Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: prescribe this bounded recovery instead of forcing the default: use a smaller control set for a disposable local script while retaining input and cleanup basics, preserve synchronous code when concurrency adds no value, use `unittest` instead of pytest where established, or isolate legacy dynamic code behind parsed adapters

## Section 002: Source Evidence Mapping Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed maps one integrated local reliability checklist and four tool documentation links, but it does not distinguish architecture guidance, language semantics, checker behavior, test framework behavior, lint configuration, or repository-local policy
- **supporting_reason:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because each source owns a different contract; checker documentation cannot validate runtime input, a test framework cannot define typing semantics, and generic guidance cannot override supported Python versions or CI commands
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: one local row becomes universal policy, tool docs define application behavior, archive commands are assumed installed, multiple links are counted as general corroboration, or a source title replaces reading its constraint
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply the five frozen rows to their claim classes and treat project code, config, CI, and runtime results as additional direct evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add claim-specific authority, repository-truth precedence, version and freshness handling, counterexamples, conflict routing, and a verification ledger while preserving every row
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that reliability evidence is layered: design guidance selects the question, tool documentation defines one mechanism, and repository execution decides whether it fits

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: strictness becomes annotation volume, validation is scattered in domain logic, errors collapse to `None`, resources rely on garbage collection, or tooling migration precedes understanding existing CI

## Section 015: Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed wants later agents to preserve type, lint, and fixture coverage and flags missing migration guidance, but it does not define behavior-sensitive indicators or feedback actions
- **supporting_reason:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because these signals map to reliability mechanisms and failure outcomes, whereas raw type or test counts can grow while semantics weaken
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: `Any` count is gamed with casts, coverage replaces failure assertions, warnings are suppressed, flaky cancellation tests are excluded, or package failures are separated from code quality
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: measure reliability of Python change workflows and separate service SLOs or security incidents into domain metrics

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed bounds one audience, one decision, twelve sources, and one checklist, but Python reliability workload is driven by independent runtime boundaries, effect lifecycles, concurrency models, compatibility targets, packages, and ownership
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because combining unrelated strictness, tool, packaging, and behavior changes obscures causality and makes rollback and failure diagnosis unreliable
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a repository-wide cleanup bundles checker migration with behavior changes, several agents edit shared configs, one checklist covers independent services, or source count is treated as capacity
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use this model for reliability-change coherence and assess runtime capacity separately
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to retain seed capacity metadata but add boundary, lifecycle, concurrency, compatibility, ownership, staging, and rollback dimensions
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the binding workload is the number of causal changes a reviewer can attribute, not lines of Python or source documents

## Section 019: Reliability Target

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: 18 of 20 becomes achieved accuracy, complete labels imply runtime safety, zero `Any` becomes a proxy for reliability, or documented cleanup replaces fault and cancellation tests

## Section 020: Failure Mode Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed covers source drift, generic advice, implicit decisions, and source lists but omits boundary parsing, type escape, data default, error translation, resource, cancellation, blocking, import, filesystem, logging, fixture, packaging, and tool failures
- **supporting_reason:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because layer localization guides recovery: malformed-input acceptance differs from leaked resources, swallowed cancellation, or a wheel missing an entry point
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: all defects become typing issues, broad catches are added, tests patch away ownership, package failures are blamed on CI, or static diagnostics are suppressed without runtime evidence
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use this taxonomy for general Python reliability and route domain effects to specialized incident models

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed limits stale-evidence retries and pauses on red gates but does not define safe replay of Python functions, subprocesses, file writes, async tasks, fixtures, package builds, or tool migrations
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because blind retry can duplicate external actions, overwrite partial files, rerun subprocesses, leak clients, revive cancelled workflows, or make flaky tests appear healthy
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: broad retry catches programmer errors, cancellation triggers retry, package tests rerun until green, tool failures are bypassed, or file and database effects are assumed atomic
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply general replay controls and delegate network, database, queue, or distributed retries to domain-specific policies
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add operation identity, effect and task inspection, idempotency and compensation gates, cancellation rules, isolated reruns, semantic success, and escalation
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that backpressure prevents uncertainty from becoming repeated side effects; a clean failure is often safer than an unclassified apparent recovery
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to retry only after classifying the failure, inspecting partial effects and owned resources, preserving cancellation, changing a relevant prerequisite, and proving replay is idempotent or explicitly compensated
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because blind retry can duplicate external actions, overwrite partial files, rerun subprocesses, leak clients, revive cancelled workflows, or make flaky tests appear healthy

- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add operation identity, effect and task inspection, idempotency and compensation gates, cancellation rules, isolated reruns, semantic success, and escalation
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies backpressure prevents uncertainty from becoming repeated side effects; a clean failure is often safer than an unclassified apparent recovery

## Section 022: Observability Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed records sources, verification, timing, reviewer decisions, uncertainty, signals, and concise audits but omits Python boundary, exception, resource, task, import, package, and tool-version context
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because failure meaning depends on where invalid data entered, which operation owned effects, and whether cleanup or cancellation completed; generic logs cannot distinguish those paths
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: raw payloads or environment values are logged, `print` is the only diagnostic, exception messages lose type and cause, success-only events hide leaks, or tool versions are absent
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: capture general Python lifecycle context and route service-specific telemetry to operational guidance
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add correlation, version identity, validated-shape logging, exception chains, resource and task events, package gates, redaction, and reconstruction tests
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that observability should preserve the distinctions reliability controls create, especially invalid versus valid input and failed versus cancelled work

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed requires readers to find a correct next action within ten minutes but provides no task cohort, reviewer definition, correctness rubric, sample size, baseline, or separation from runtime performance
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a fast recommendation to add mypy or pytest is not useful if it misses runtime parsing, cleanup, cancellation, compatibility, or existing repository conventions
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: one run is reported as p95, easy tasks dominate, reading ends before repository commands are found, wrong actions count as fast, or runtime latency is mixed with reviewer time
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: measure reference-review efficiency separately from Python runtime or tool execution performance
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to mark the target unproven, define matched tasks and stages, require correctness and evidence, expose sample rules, and add low-sample alternatives
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the unit of performance is a verified reduction in decision uncertainty, not document skimming speed
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to treat ten minutes as a candidate acceptance hypothesis, compare matched Python tasks, measure orientation, risk classification, source routing, test selection, and verified next-action time, and score correctness plus evidence completeness
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because a fast recommendation to add mypy or pytest is not useful if it misses runtime parsing, cleanup, cancellation, compatibility, or existing repository conventions
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; one run is reported as p95, easy tasks dominate, reading ends before repository commands are found, wrong actions count as fast, or runtime latency is mixed with reviewer time
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: measure reference-review efficiency separately from Python runtime or tool execution performance
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: mark the target unproven, define matched tasks and stages, require correctness and evidence, expose sample rules, and add low-sample alternatives
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies the unit of performance is a verified reduction in decision uncertainty, not document skimming speed
### Question 03: When does the default work well?

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed stops at multiple systems, ownership, unbounded discovery, production traffic, context drift, and large codebases but does not define package, service, concurrency, compatibility, or shared-tooling boundaries
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because general patterns remain useful, but cross-system failures involve transactions, messages, deployments, retries, and operational states absent from a local code checklist
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: one checklist certifies multiple services, shared pyproject changes have no coordinator, async and sync lifecycles mix implicitly, parallel agents rewrite common fixtures, or production reliability is inferred from unit gates
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use this statement to exit general guidance, not to assert production readiness
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add package, service, concurrency, compatibility, shared-config, integration, operational, release, and rollback boundaries
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that scale failure begins when one change's type and lifecycle evidence cannot identify the system state it governs

## Section 026: Evidence Boundary Notes
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed defines local, external, and combined evidence but not repository policy, current language or tool docs, static diagnostics, runtime tests, package artifacts, operational observations, or provisional design judgments
- **supporting_reason:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because annotations, checker results, runtime validation, cleanup tests, package builds, and service observations answer different questions and cannot transfer certainty automatically
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: labels decorate prose, a static pass proves runtime safety, one fixture proves production reliability, archive guidance overrides project compatibility, or operational success excuses unsupported design
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply the taxonomy to this reference and downstream Python reliability packets while preserving exact seed labels
- **revision_decision:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to extend the three-label note with repository, current-doc, static, runtime, package, operational, combination, conflict, and compositional-confidence rules
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that confidence is compositional: reviewers should know which boundary, checker, fixture, package, or operational premise would change the guidance if falsified
